## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction system. The rate law typically depends on the concentration A (through power-law or rational forms), and may depend explicitly on time t for non-autonomous systems like photolysis or time-varying conditions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction or constant source)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., photolysis)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Combined source-sink: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (polynomial rate law with production and consumption)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order kinetics with constant flux)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is linearly proportional to A, this indicates first-order kinetics (exponential decay/growth of concentration)
- If dA_dt depends on A but not explicitly on t, the system is autonomous and follows a standard rate law
- A quadratic dependence on A (A² term) suggests bimolecular reactions where two molecules of the same species react
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate saturation or enzyme-mediated mechanisms where binding sites become limiting
- If dA_dt has an explicit time dependence beyond what A(t) provides, this suggests externally driven conditions (varying temperature, light intensity, or catalyst activity)
- A product form A*(c-A) indicates autocatalytic or logistic behavior where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- A constant additive term in the rate law suggests a zeroth-order production or an external feed of reactant into the system
- Negative values of dA_dt with magnitude increasing with A suggest consumption kinetics (reactant being used up)
- If the rate law involves A raised to a non-integer power, this may indicate complex multi-step reaction mechanisms or fractal kinetics
- Denominator terms like (1+c*A)^n suggest adsorption or inhibition effects where high concentration reduces effective reaction rate

**GT:** `0.7391218893246799*A**2/(0.8913296033617462*A**4 + 1) - 0.3009370469546767*A*exp(-0.06776739623123975*t)`

This has two terms:
1. A rational term: `k * A**2 / (m * A**4 + 1)`
2. An exponential decay term: `-c * A * exp(-d*t)`

Let me analyze each candidate for potential equivalence.

**Key structural requirements:**
- Need `A*exp(αt)` term (the exponential decay)
- Need `A²/(A⁴ + const)` term (the rational function)

The rational term `A²/(cA⁴+1)` is crucial. This is NOT equivalent to a polynomial in A, nor to simple `1/(A+c)` forms, nor to exponentials in A.

**Candidate 18:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2/(A**c1 + c3) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7/A`

Setting c0=0, c4=0, c7=0: `A**c1*c2/(A**c1 + c3) + c5*exp(c6*t)`

The term `A**c1*c2/(A**c1 + c3)` — if I set c1=2, this becomes `A²*c2/(A² + c3)`. But I need `A²/(A⁴ + const)`. These aren't the same. `A²/(A⁴+1) = 1/(A² + 1/A²)` — not the same as `A²/(A²+c)`.

If c1=4: `A⁴*c2/(A⁴ + c3)` = `c2 - c2*c3/(A⁴+c3)`. Not `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

**Candidate 29:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7/(A + c8)`

The `A**c1*c2*exp(c3*t)` with c1=1 gives `A*c2*exp(c3*t)` ✓ for the exponential term. But `c7/(A+c8)` can't produce `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

**Candidate 22:** `A**c0*c1 + A**c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + A**c5*c6*t**c7 + c8*t*exp(A*c9)`

Setting c9=0, c8*t term remains — problematic. Can't eliminate t dependence there properly.

**Candidate 35:** `A**2*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2 + A*c3/(A + c4) + A*c5/(A*c6 + c7) + c8/(A*c6 + c7) + c9`

Setting c1=0 (so first term is `A²*c0`), this gives polynomials and rational terms like `A/(A+c)` which are `1 - c/(A+c)`. Can't produce `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

None of these simple rational forms `1/(A+c)`, `A/(A+c)²`, etc. can produce `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

**Candidate 11:** `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(A*c3 + c4*t) + A + A**c5*c6*exp(c7*t) + c8`

After extensive analysis, none of the candidates contain the structure needed to produce `A²/(A⁴ + const)`. This rational function requires either:
- An explicit `A²/(A⁴+c)` form, or
- Some algebraic identity that can produce it.

No candidate has `A^n` in both numerator and denominator with the right structure to create `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

- `A/(A+c)` is NOT equivalent

Let me check each candidate systematically:

**Candidates with `A*c/(A+c)` type terms** (4,6,7,9,12,14,25,35,36,37,42,44,45,47): These produce rational functions like `A/(A+c)` or `1/(A+c)` or `A/(A+c)²` or `1/(A²+c)`. None can produce `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

**Candidates with exponentials in A** (3,10,13,26,27,30,31,34,40,41,43,47,49): Terms like `exp(A*c)` are not equivalent to rational functions of A.

**Candidates with log terms** (2,5,8,15,16,28,38,48,50): `log(A*c+1)` cannot produce `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

**Candidates with cos/sin** (1,2,20,23,24,40,41,46): Trigonometric functions can't produce rational functions.

**Candidate 18:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2/(A**c1 + c3) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7/A`

Setting c1=2: `A²*c2/(A²+c3)`. This gives `A²/(A²+c)`, NOT `A²/(A⁴+c)`. Not equivalent.

**Candidate 29:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7/(A+c8)`

The `A**c1*exp(c3*t)` with c1=1 gives the exponential term. But `1/(A+c)` cannot give `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

**Candidate 21, 22, 46:** These have `A**c0*c1` type terms but no rational function of A⁴.

**Candidate 35:** Has `A³/(A+c)` type terms — not equivalent.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain a term that can produce the rational function `A²/(A⁴+1)`. This specific rational structure requires A⁴ in the denominator, which no candidate provides. The closest are `1/(A²+c)` (candidates 14, 32) or `A^c/(A^c+c)` (candidate 18 with max A²), but none match.
